     </table> 
     <p><b>Bioinformatics</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/76/En-us-bioinformatics.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11"></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-bioinformatics.ogg" title="File:En-us-bioinformatics.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> is an <a href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary" title="Interdisciplinary" class="mw-redirect">interdisciplinary</a> field that develops methods and software tools for understanding <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biological</a> data. As an interdisciplinary field of science, bioinformatics combines <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> to analyze and interpret <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biological</a> data. Bioinformatics has been used for <i><a href="/wiki/In_silico" title="In silico">in silico</a></i> analyses of <a href="/wiki/Biological" title="Biological" class="mw-redirect">biological</a> queries using <a href="/wiki/Mathematical" title="Mathematical" class="mw-redirect">mathematical</a> and statistical techniques.</p> 
     <p>Bioinformatics is both an umbrella term for the body of biological studies that use computer programming as part of their methodology, as well as a reference to specific analysis "pipelines" that are repeatedly used, particularly in the field of <a href="/wiki/Genomics" title="Genomics">genomics</a>. Common uses of bioinformatics include the identification of candidate genes and nucleotides (SNPs). Often, such identification is made with the aim of better understanding the genetic basis of disease, unique adaptations, desirable properties (esp. in agricultural species), or differences between populations. In a less formal way, bioinformatics also tries to understand the organisational principles within <a href="/wiki/Nucleic_acid" title="Nucleic acid">nucleic acid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a> sequences.</p> 
     <p></p>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduction">Introduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Introduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Bioinformatics has become an important part of many areas of biology. In experimental molecular biology, bioinformatics techniques such as image and <a href="/wiki/Signal_processing" title="Signal processing">signal processing</a> allow extraction of useful results from large amounts of raw data. In the field of genetics and genomics, it aids in sequencing and annotating genomes and their observed <a href="/wiki/Mutation" title="Mutation">mutations</a>. It plays a role in the <a href="/wiki/Text_mining" title="Text mining">text mining</a> of biological literature and the development of biological and gene ontologies to organize and query biological data. It also plays a role in the analysis of gene and protein expression and regulation. Bioinformatics tools aid in the comparison of genetic and genomic data and more generally in the understanding of evolutionary aspects of molecular biology. At a more integrative level, it helps analyze and catalogue the biological pathways and networks that are an important part of systems biology. In structural biology, it aids in the simulation and modeling of DNA, RNA, and protein structures as well as molecular interactions.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Historically, the term <i>bioinformatics</i> did not mean what it means today. <a href="/wiki/Paulien_Hogeweg" title="Paulien Hogeweg">Paulien Hogeweg</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Hesper&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ben Hesper (page does not exist)">Ben Hesper</a> coined it in 1970 to refer to the study of information processes in biotic systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Hogeweg2011_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogeweg2011-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> This definition placed bioinformatics as a field parallel to <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">biophysics</a> (the study of physical processes in biological systems) or <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a> (the study of chemical processes in biological systems).<sup id="cite_ref-Hogeweg2011_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogeweg2011-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequences">Sequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png/220px-Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png" width="220" height="63" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png/330px-Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png/440px-Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="153"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Image_DNA_sequence_-_png.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Sequences of genetic material are frequently used in bioinformatics and are easier to manage using computers than manually.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Computers became essential in molecular biology when <a href="/wiki/Protein_sequences" title="Protein sequences" class="mw-redirect">protein sequences</a> became available after <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Sanger" title="Frederick Sanger">Frederick Sanger</a> determined the sequence of <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a> in the early 1950s. Comparing multiple sequences manually turned out to be impractical. A pioneer in the field was <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Oakley_Dayhoff" title="Margaret Oakley Dayhoff">Margaret Oakley Dayhoff</a>, who has been hailed by <a href="/wiki/David_Lipman" title="David Lipman" class="mw-redirect">David Lipman</a>, director of the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Biotechnology_Information" title="National Center for Biotechnology Information">National Center for Biotechnology Information</a>, as the "mother and father of bioinformatics."<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Dayhoff compiled one of the first protein sequence databases, initially published as books<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> and pioneered methods of sequence alignment and molecular evolution.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid17775169_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17775169-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Another early contributor to bioinformatics was <a href="/wiki/Elvin_A._Kabat" title="Elvin A. Kabat">Elvin A. Kabat</a>, who pioneered biological sequence analysis in 1970 with his comprehensive volumes of antibody sequences released with Tai Te Wu between 1980 and 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goals">Goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>To study how normal cellular activities are altered in different disease states, the biological data must be combined to form a comprehensive picture of these activities. Therefore, the field of bioinformatics has evolved such that the most pressing task now involves the analysis and interpretation of various types of data. This includes nucleotide and amino acid sequences, <a href="/wiki/Protein_domain" title="Protein domain">protein domains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protein_structure" title="Protein structure">protein structures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The actual process of analyzing and interpreting data is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Computational_biology" title="Computational biology">computational biology</a>. Important sub-disciplines within bioinformatics and computational biology include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Development and implementation of computer programs that enable efficient access to, use and management of, various types of information</li> 
      <li>Development of new algorithms (mathematical formulas) and statistical measures that assess relationships among members of large data sets. For example, there are methods to locate a <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">gene</a> within a sequence, to predict protein structure and/or function, and to <a href="/wiki/Cluster_analysis" title="Cluster analysis">cluster</a> protein sequences into families of related sequences.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The primary goal of bioinformatics is to increase the understanding of biological processes. What sets it apart from other approaches, however, is its focus on developing and applying computationally intensive techniques to achieve this goal. Examples include: <a href="/wiki/Pattern_recognition" title="Pattern recognition">pattern recognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_mining" title="Data mining">data mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a> algorithms, and <a href="/wiki/Biological_Data_Visualization" title="Biological Data Visualization" class="mw-redirect">visualization</a>. Major research efforts in the field include <a href="/wiki/Sequence_alignment" title="Sequence alignment">sequence alignment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gene_finding" title="Gene finding" class="mw-redirect">gene finding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genome_assembly" title="Genome assembly" class="mw-redirect">genome assembly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug_design" title="Drug design">drug design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug_discovery" title="Drug discovery">drug discovery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protein_structural_alignment" title="Protein structural alignment" class="mw-redirect">protein structure alignment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protein_structure_prediction" title="Protein structure prediction">protein structure prediction</a>, prediction of <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">gene expression</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein%E2%80%93protein_interactions" title="Protein–protein interactions" class="mw-redirect">protein–protein interactions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genome-wide_association_studies" title="Genome-wide association studies" class="mw-redirect">genome-wide association studies</a>, the modeling of <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cellular_model" title="Cellular model">cell division/mitosis.</a></p> 
     <p>Bioinformatics now entails the creation and advancement of databases, algorithms, computational and statistical techniques, and theory to solve formal and practical problems arising from the management and analysis of biological data.</p> 
     <p>Over the past few decades, rapid developments in genomic and other molecular research technologies and developments in information technologies have combined to produce a tremendous amount of information related to molecular biology. Bioinformatics is the name given to these mathematical and computing approaches used to glean understanding of biological processes.</p> 
     <p>Common activities in bioinformatics include mapping and analyzing <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> and protein sequences, aligning DNA and protein sequences to compare them, and creating and viewing 3-D models of protein structures.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relation_to_other_fields">Relation to other fields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Relation to other fields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Bioinformatics is a science field that is similar to but distinct from <a href="/wiki/Biological_computation" title="Biological computation">biological computation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computational_biology" title="Computational biology">computational biology</a>. Biological computation uses <a href="/wiki/Bioengineering" title="Bioengineering" class="mw-redirect">bioengineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> to build biological <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, whereas bioinformatics uses computation to better understand biology. Bioinformatics and computational biology have similar aims and approaches, but they differ in scale: bioinformatics organizes and analyzes basic biological data, whereas computational biology builds theoretical models of biological systems, just as <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_biology" title="Mathematical biology" class="mw-redirect">mathematical biology</a> does with mathematical models.</p> 
     <p>Analyzing biological data to produce meaningful information involves writing and running software programs that use <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> from <a href="/wiki/Graph_theory" title="Graph theory">graph theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soft_computing" title="Soft computing">soft computing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_mining" title="Data mining">data mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Image_processing" title="Image processing">image processing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">computer simulation</a>. The algorithms in turn depend on theoretical foundations such as <a href="/wiki/Discrete_mathematics" title="Discrete mathematics">discrete mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Control_theory" title="Control theory">control theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/System_theory" title="System theory" class="mw-redirect">system theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_theory" title="Information theory">information theory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequence_analysis">Sequence analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sequence analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_alignment" title="Sequence alignment">Sequence alignment</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_database" title="Sequence database">Sequence database</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WPP_domain_alignment.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/WPP_domain_alignment.PNG/500px-WPP_domain_alignment.PNG" width="500" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/WPP_domain_alignment.PNG/750px-WPP_domain_alignment.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/WPP_domain_alignment.PNG 2x" data-file-width="921" data-file-height="214"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WPP_domain_alignment.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The sequences of different genes or proteins may be aligned side-by-side to measure their similarity. This alignment compares protein sequences containing 
        <a href="/wiki/WPP_domain" title="WPP domain">WPP domains</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Phi_X_174" title="Phi X 174">Phage Φ-X174</a> was <a href="/wiki/Sequencing" title="Sequencing">sequenced</a> in 1977,<sup id="cite_ref-pmid870828_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid870828-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequence" title="DNA sequence" class="mw-redirect">DNA sequences</a> of thousands of organisms have been decoded and stored in databases. This sequence information is analyzed to determine genes that encode <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a>, RNA genes, regulatory sequences, structural motifs, and repetitive sequences. A comparison of genes within a <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> or between different species can show similarities between protein functions, or relations between species (the use of <a href="/wiki/Molecular_systematics" title="Molecular systematics" class="mw-redirect">molecular systematics</a> to construct <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">phylogenetic trees</a>). With the growing amount of data, it long ago became impractical to analyze DNA sequences manually. Today, <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">computer programs</a> such as <a href="/wiki/BLAST" title="BLAST">BLAST</a> are used daily to search sequences from more than 260 000 organisms, containing over 190 billion <a href="/wiki/Nucleotides" title="Nucleotides" class="mw-redirect">nucleotides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid18073190_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18073190-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> These programs can compensate for mutations (exchanged, deleted or inserted bases) in the DNA sequence, to identify sequences that are related, but not identical. A variant of this <a href="/wiki/Sequence_alignment" title="Sequence alignment">sequence alignment</a> is used in the sequencing process itself. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Shotgun_sequencing" title="Shotgun sequencing">shotgun sequencing</a> technique (which was used, for example, by <a href="/wiki/The_Institute_for_Genomic_Research" title="The Institute for Genomic Research" class="mw-redirect">The Institute for Genomic Research</a> (TIGR) to sequence the first bacterial genome, <i><a href="/wiki/Haemophilus_influenzae" title="Haemophilus influenzae">Haemophilus influenzae</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-pmid7542800_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid7542800-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> does not produce entire chromosomes. Instead it generates the sequences of many thousands of small DNA fragments (ranging from 35 to 900 nucleotides long, depending on the sequencing technology). The ends of these fragments overlap and, when aligned properly by a genome assembly program, can be used to reconstruct the complete genome. Shotgun sequencing yields sequence data quickly, but the task of assembling the fragments can be quite complicated for larger genomes. For a genome as large as the <a href="/wiki/Human_genome" title="Human genome">human genome</a>, it may take many days of CPU time on large-memory, multiprocessor computers to assemble the fragments, and the resulting assembly usually contains numerous gaps that must be filled in later. Shotgun sequencing is the method of choice for virtually all genomes sequenced today, and genome assembly algorithms are a critical area of bioinformatics research.</p> 
     <p>Following the goals that the Human Genome Project left to achieve after its closure in 2003, a new project developed by the National Human Genome Research Institute in the U.S appeared. The so-called ENCODE project is a collaborative data collection of the functional elements of the human genome that uses next-generation DNA-sequencing technologies and genomic tiling arrays, technologies able to generate automatically large amounts of data with lower research costs but with the same quality and viability.</p> 
     <p>Another aspect of bioinformatics in sequence analysis is annotation. This involves computational <a href="/wiki/Gene_finding" title="Gene finding" class="mw-redirect">gene finding</a> to search for protein-coding genes, RNA genes, and other functional sequences within a genome. Not all of the nucleotides within a genome are part of genes. Within the genomes of higher organisms, large parts of the DNA do not serve any obvious purpose.</p> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_analysis" title="Sequence analysis">sequence analysis</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_mining" title="Sequence mining" class="mw-redirect">sequence mining</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_profiling_tool" title="Sequence profiling tool">sequence profiling tool</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Sequence_motif" title="Sequence motif">sequence motif</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genome_annotation">Genome annotation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Genome annotation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Gene_prediction" title="Gene prediction">Gene prediction</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In the context of <a href="/wiki/Genomics" title="Genomics">genomics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genome_project#Genome_annotation" title="Genome project">annotation</a> is the process of marking the genes and other biological features in a DNA sequence. This process needs to be automated because most genomes are too large to annotate by hand, not to mention the desire to annotate as many genomes as possible, as the rate of <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">sequencing</a> has ceased to pose a bottleneck. Annotation is made possible by the fact that genes have recognisable start and stop regions, although the exact sequence found in these regions can vary between genes.</p> 
     <p>The first genome annotation software system was designed in 1995 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Owen_White&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Owen White (page does not exist)">Owen White</a>, who was part of the team at <a href="/wiki/The_Institute_for_Genomic_Research" title="The Institute for Genomic Research" class="mw-redirect">The Institute for Genomic Research</a> that sequenced and analyzed the first genome of a free-living organism to be decoded, the bacterium <i><a href="/wiki/Haemophilus_influenzae" title="Haemophilus influenzae">Haemophilus influenzae</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid7542800_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid7542800-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> White built a software system to find the genes (fragments of genomic sequence that encode proteins), the transfer RNAs, and to make initial assignments of function to those genes. Most current genome annotation systems work similarly, but the programs available for analysis of genomic DNA, such as the <a href="/wiki/GeneMark" title="GeneMark">GeneMark</a> program trained and used to find protein-coding genes in <i><a href="/wiki/Haemophilus_influenzae" title="Haemophilus influenzae">Haemophilus influenzae</a></i>, are constantly changing and improving.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computational_evolutionary_biology">Computational evolutionary biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Computational evolutionary biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_biology" title="Evolutionary biology">Evolutionary biology</a> is the study of the origin and descent of <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, as well as their change over time. <a href="/wiki/Informatics_(academic_field)" title="Informatics (academic field)" class="mw-redirect">Informatics</a> has assisted evolutionary biologists by enabling researchers to:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>trace the evolution of a large number of organisms by measuring changes in their <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>, rather than through physical taxonomy or physiological observations alone,</li> 
      <li>more recently, compare entire <a href="/wiki/Genomes" title="Genomes" class="mw-redirect">genomes</a>, which permits the study of more complex evolutionary events, such as <a href="/wiki/Gene_duplication" title="Gene duplication">gene duplication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_gene_transfer" title="Horizontal gene transfer">horizontal gene transfer</a>, and the prediction of factors important in bacterial <a href="/wiki/Speciation" title="Speciation">speciation</a>,</li> 
      <li>build complex computational models of populations to predict the outcome of the system over time<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>track and share information on an increasingly large number of species and organisms</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Future work endeavours to reconstruct the now more complex <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_tree" title="Evolutionary tree" class="mw-redirect">tree of life</a>.</p> 
     <p>The area of research within <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> that uses <a href="/wiki/Genetic_algorithm" title="Genetic algorithm">genetic algorithms</a> is sometimes confused with computational evolutionary biology, but the two areas are not necessarily related.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparative_genomics">Comparative genomics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Comparative genomics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Comparative_genomics" title="Comparative genomics">Comparative genomics</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The core of comparative genome analysis is the establishment of the correspondence between <a href="/wiki/Genes" title="Genes" class="mw-redirect">genes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Homology_(biology)#Orthology" title="Homology (biology)">orthology</a> analysis) or other genomic features in different organisms. It is these intergenomic maps that make it possible to trace the evolutionary processes responsible for the divergence of two genomes. A multitude of evolutionary events acting at various organizational levels shape genome evolution. At the lowest level, point mutations affect individual nucleotides. At a higher level, large chromosomal segments undergo duplication, lateral transfer, inversion, transposition, deletion and insertion.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Ultimately, whole genomes are involved in processes of hybridization, polyploidization and <a href="/wiki/Endosymbiosis" title="Endosymbiosis" class="mw-redirect">endosymbiosis</a>, often leading to rapid speciation. The complexity of genome evolution poses many exciting challenges to developers of mathematical models and algorithms, who have recourse to a spectra of algorithmic, statistical and mathematical techniques, ranging from exact, <a href="/wiki/Heuristics" title="Heuristics" class="mw-redirect">heuristics</a>, fixed parameter and <a href="/wiki/Approximation_algorithms" title="Approximation algorithms" class="mw-redirect">approximation algorithms</a> for problems based on parsimony models to <a href="/wiki/Markov_Chain_Monte_Carlo" title="Markov Chain Monte Carlo" class="mw-redirect">Markov Chain Monte Carlo</a> algorithms for <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_analysis" title="Bayesian analysis" class="mw-redirect">Bayesian analysis</a> of problems based on probabilistic models.</p> 
     <p>Many of these studies are based on the <a href="/wiki/Homology_(biology)" title="Homology (biology)">homology</a> detection and protein families computation.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pan_genomics">Pan genomics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pan genomics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pan-genome" title="Pan-genome">Pan-genome</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Pan genomics is a concept introduced in 2005 by Tettelin and Medini which eventually took root in bioinformatics. Pan genome is the complete gene repertoire of a particular taxonomic group: although initially applied to closely related strains of a species, it can be applied to a larger context like genus, phylum etc. It is divided in two parts- The Core genome: Set of genes common to all the genomes under study (These are often housekeeping genes vital for survival) and The Dispensable/Flexible Genome: Set of genes not present in all but one or some genomes under study.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics_of_disease">Genetics of disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Genetics of disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Genome-wide_association_studies" title="Genome-wide association studies" class="mw-redirect">Genome-wide association studies</a>
     </div> 
     <p>With the advent of next-generation sequencing we are obtaining enough sequence data to map the genes of complex diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Infertility" title="Infertility">infertility</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Demerec1945_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demerec1945-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a><sup id="cite_ref-V.C3.A9ron2013_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V.C3.A9ron2013-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_Disease" title="Alzheimer's Disease" class="mw-redirect">Alzheimer's Disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tosto2013_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tosto2013-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Genome-wide association studies are a useful approach to pinpoint the mutations responsible for such complex diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-Londin2013_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Londin2013-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Through these studies, thousands of DNA variants have been identified that are associated with similar diseases and traits.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Furthermore, the possibility for genes to be used at prognosis, diagnosis or treatment is one of the most essential applications. Many studies are discussing both the promising ways to choose the genes to be used and the problems and pitfalls of using genes to predict disease presence or prognosis.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_mutations_in_cancer">Analysis of mutations in cancer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Analysis of mutations in cancer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Oncogenomics" title="Oncogenomics">Oncogenomics</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, the genomes of affected cells are rearranged in complex or even unpredictable ways. Massive sequencing efforts are used to identify previously unknown <a href="/wiki/Point_mutation" title="Point mutation">point mutations</a> in a variety of <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> in cancer. Bioinformaticians continue to produce specialized automated systems to manage the sheer volume of sequence data produced, and they create new algorithms and software to compare the sequencing results to the growing collection of <a href="/wiki/Human_genome" title="Human genome">human genome</a> sequences and <a href="/wiki/Germline" title="Germline">germline</a> polymorphisms. New physical detection technologies are employed, such as <a href="/wiki/Oligonucleotide" title="Oligonucleotide">oligonucleotide</a> microarrays to identify chromosomal gains and losses (called <a href="/wiki/Comparative_genomic_hybridization" title="Comparative genomic hybridization">comparative genomic hybridization</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Single-nucleotide_polymorphism" title="Single-nucleotide polymorphism">single-nucleotide polymorphism</a> arrays to detect known <i>point mutations</i>. These detection methods simultaneously measure several hundred thousand sites throughout the genome, and when used in high-throughput to measure thousands of samples, generate <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" title="Terabyte">terabytes</a> of data per experiment. Again the massive amounts and new types of data generate new opportunities for bioinformaticians. The data is often found to contain considerable variability, or <a href="/wiki/Noise" title="Noise">noise</a>, and thus <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Markov_model" title="Hidden Markov model">Hidden Markov model</a> and change-point analysis methods are being developed to infer real <a href="/wiki/Copy_number_variation" title="Copy number variation" class="mw-redirect">copy number</a> changes.</p> 
     <p>However, with the breakthroughs that the next-generation sequencing technology is providing to the field of Bioinformatics, cancer genomics may be drastically change. This new methods and software allow bioinformaticians to sequence in a rapid and affordable way many cancer genomes. This could mean a more flexible process to classify types of cancer by analysis of cancer driven mutations in the genome. Furthermore, individual tracking of patients during the progression of the disease may be possible in the future with the sequence of cancer samples.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another type of data that requires novel informatics development is the analysis of <a href="/wiki/Lesion" title="Lesion">lesions</a> found to be recurrent among many tumors.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gene_and_protein_expression">Gene and protein expression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gene and protein expression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_gene_expression">Analysis of gene expression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Analysis of gene expression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">expression</a> of many genes can be determined by measuring <a href="/wiki/Messenger_RNA" title="Messenger RNA">mRNA</a> levels with multiple techniques including <a href="/wiki/DNA_microarray" title="DNA microarray">microarrays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressed_sequence_tag" title="Expressed sequence tag">expressed cDNA sequence tag</a> (EST) sequencing, <a href="/wiki/Serial_analysis_of_gene_expression" title="Serial analysis of gene expression">serial analysis of gene expression</a> (SAGE) tag sequencing, <a href="/wiki/Massively_parallel_signature_sequencing" title="Massively parallel signature sequencing">massively parallel signature sequencing</a> (MPSS), <a href="/wiki/RNA-Seq" title="RNA-Seq">RNA-Seq</a>, also known as "Whole Transcriptome Shotgun Sequencing" (WTSS), or various applications of multiplexed in-situ hybridization. All of these techniques are extremely noise-prone and/or subject to bias in the biological measurement, and a major research area in computational biology involves developing statistical tools to separate <a href="/wiki/Signal_(information_theory)" title="Signal (information theory)" class="mw-redirect">signal</a> from <a href="/wiki/Noise" title="Noise">noise</a> in high-throughput gene expression studies. Such studies are often used to determine the genes implicated in a disorder: one might compare microarray data from cancerous <a href="/wiki/Epithelial" title="Epithelial" class="mw-redirect">epithelial</a> cells to data from non-cancerous cells to determine the transcripts that are up-regulated and down-regulated in a particular population of cancer cells.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_protein_expression">Analysis of protein expression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Analysis of protein expression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Protein_microarray" title="Protein microarray">Protein microarrays</a> and high throughput (HT) <a href="/wiki/Mass_spectrometry" title="Mass spectrometry">mass spectrometry</a> (MS) can provide a snapshot of the proteins present in a biological sample. Bioinformatics is very much involved in making sense of protein microarray and HT MS data; the former approach faces similar problems as with microarrays targeted at mRNA, the latter involves the problem of matching large amounts of mass data against predicted masses from protein sequence databases, and the complicated statistical analysis of samples where multiple, but incomplete peptides from each protein are detected.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_regulation">Analysis of regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Analysis of regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Regulation is the complex orchestration of events starting with an extracellular signal such as a <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">hormone</a> and leading to an increase or decrease in the activity of one or more <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a>. Bioinformatics techniques have been applied to explore various steps in this process. For example, promoter analysis involves the identification and study of <a href="/wiki/Sequence_motif" title="Sequence motif">sequence motifs</a> in the DNA surrounding the coding region of a gene. These motifs influence the extent to which that region is transcribed into mRNA. Expression data can be used to infer gene regulation: one might compare <a href="/wiki/Microarray" title="Microarray">microarray</a> data from a wide variety of states of an organism to form hypotheses about the genes involved in each state. In a single-cell organism, one might compare stages of the <a href="/wiki/Cell_cycle" title="Cell cycle">cell cycle</a>, along with various stress conditions (heat shock, starvation, etc.). One can then apply <a href="/wiki/Cluster_analysis" title="Cluster analysis">clustering algorithms</a> to that expression data to determine which genes are co-expressed. For example, the upstream regions (promoters) of co-expressed genes can be searched for over-represented <a href="/wiki/Regulatory_elements" title="Regulatory elements" class="mw-redirect">regulatory elements</a>. Examples of clustering algorithms applied in gene clustering are <a href="/wiki/K-means_clustering" title="K-means clustering">k-means clustering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Self-organizing_map" title="Self-organizing map">self-organizing maps</a> (SOMs), <a href="/wiki/Hierarchical_clustering" title="Hierarchical clustering">hierarchical clustering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consensus_clustering" title="Consensus clustering">consensus clustering</a> methods such as the <a href="/wiki/Bi-CoPaM" title="Bi-CoPaM" class="mw-redirect">Bi-CoPaM</a>. The later, namely <a href="/wiki/Bi-CoPaM" title="Bi-CoPaM" class="mw-redirect">Bi-CoPaM</a>, has been actually proposed to address various issues specific to gene discovery problems such as consistent co-expression of genes over multiple microarray datasets.<sup id="cite_ref-AbuJamousPLOSONE_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AbuJamousPLOSONE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AbuJamousInterface_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AbuJamousInterface-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_bioinformatics">Structural bioinformatics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Structural bioinformatics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Structural_bioinformatics" title="Structural bioinformatics">Structural bioinformatics</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Protein_structure_prediction" title="Protein structure prediction">Protein structure prediction</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Structural_motif" title="Structural motif">Structural motif</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Structural_domain" title="Structural domain" class="mw-redirect">Structural domain</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1kqf_opm.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1kqf_opm.png/220px-1kqf_opm.png" width="220" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1kqf_opm.png/330px-1kqf_opm.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1kqf_opm.png/440px-1kqf_opm.png 2x" data-file-width="626" data-file-height="745"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1kqf_opm.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 3-dimensional protein structures such as this one are common subjects in bioinformatic analyses.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Protein structure prediction is another important application of bioinformatics. The <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">amino acid</a> sequence of a protein, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Primary_structure" title="Primary structure" class="mw-redirect">primary structure</a>, can be easily determined from the sequence on the gene that codes for it. In the vast majority of cases, this primary structure uniquely determines a structure in its native environment. (Of course, there are exceptions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bovine_spongiform_encephalopathy" title="Bovine spongiform encephalopathy">bovine spongiform encephalopathy</a> – a.k.a. <a href="/wiki/Mad_Cow_Disease" title="Mad Cow Disease" class="mw-redirect">Mad Cow Disease</a> – <a href="/wiki/Prion" title="Prion">prion</a>.) Knowledge of this structure is vital in understanding the function of the protein. Structural information is usually classified as one of <i><a href="/wiki/Secondary_structure" title="Secondary structure" class="mw-redirect">secondary</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tertiary_structure" title="Tertiary structure" class="mw-redirect">tertiary</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Quaternary_structure" title="Quaternary structure" class="mw-redirect">quaternary</a></i> structure. A viable general solution to such predictions remains an open problem. Most efforts have so far been directed towards heuristics that work most of the time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>One of the key ideas in bioinformatics is the notion of <a href="/wiki/Homology_(biology)" title="Homology (biology)">homology</a>. In the genomic branch of bioinformatics, homology is used to predict the function of a gene: if the sequence of gene <i>A</i>, whose function is known, is homologous to the sequence of gene <i>B,</i> whose function is unknown, one could infer that B may share A's function. In the structural branch of bioinformatics, homology is used to determine which parts of a protein are important in structure formation and interaction with other proteins. In a technique called homology modeling, this information is used to predict the structure of a protein once the structure of a homologous protein is known. This currently remains the only way to predict protein structures reliably.</p> 
     <p>One example of this is the similar protein homology between hemoglobin in humans and the hemoglobin in legumes (<a href="/wiki/Leghemoglobin" title="Leghemoglobin">leghemoglobin</a>). Both serve the same purpose of transporting oxygen in the organism. Though both of these proteins have completely different amino acid sequences, their protein structures are virtually identical, which reflects their near identical purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other techniques for predicting protein structure include protein threading and <i>de novo</i> (from scratch) physics-based modeling.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Network_and_systems_biology">Network and systems biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Network and systems biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Computational_systems_biology" title="Computational systems biology" class="mw-redirect">Computational systems biology</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Biological_network" title="Biological network">Biological network</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Interactome" title="Interactome">Interactome</a>
     </div> 
     <p><i>Network analysis</i> seeks to understand the relationships within <a href="/wiki/Biological_network" title="Biological network">biological networks</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_network" title="Metabolic network">metabolic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Interactome" title="Interactome">protein-protein interaction networks</a>. Although biological networks can be constructed from a single type of molecule or entity (such as genes), network biology often attempts to integrate many different data types, such as proteins, small molecules, gene expression data, and others, which are all connected physically, functionally, or both.</p> 
     <p><i>Systems biology</i> involves the use of <a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">computer simulations</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cellular</a> subsystems (such as the <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_network" title="Metabolic network">networks of metabolites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzymes</a> that comprise <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">metabolism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Signal_transduction" title="Signal transduction">signal transduction</a> pathways and <a href="/wiki/Gene_regulatory_network" title="Gene regulatory network">gene regulatory networks</a>) to both analyze and visualize the complex connections of these cellular processes. <a href="/wiki/Artificial_life" title="Artificial life">Artificial life</a> or virtual evolution attempts to understand evolutionary processes via the computer simulation of simple (artificial) life forms.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Molecular_interaction_networks">Molecular interaction networks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Molecular interaction networks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png/200px-The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png" width="200" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png/300px-The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png/400px-The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png 2x" data-file-width="1534" data-file-height="1444"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_protein_interaction_network_of_Treponema_pallidum.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Interactions between proteins are frequently visualized and analyzed using networks. This network is made up of protein-protein interactions from 
        <i><a href="/wiki/Treponema_pallidum" title="Treponema pallidum">Treponema pallidum</a></i>, the causative agent of 
        <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a> and other diseases.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Protein%E2%80%93protein_interaction_prediction" title="Protein–protein interaction prediction">Protein–protein interaction prediction</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Interactome" title="Interactome">interactome</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Tens of thousands of three-dimensional protein structures have been determined by <a href="/wiki/X-ray_crystallography" title="X-ray crystallography">X-ray crystallography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein_nuclear_magnetic_resonance_spectroscopy" title="Protein nuclear magnetic resonance spectroscopy" class="mw-redirect">protein nuclear magnetic resonance spectroscopy</a> (protein NMR) and a central question in structural bioinformatics is whether it is practical to predict possible protein–protein interactions only based on these 3D shapes, without performing <a href="/wiki/Protein%E2%80%93protein_interaction" title="Protein–protein interaction">protein–protein interaction</a> experiments. A variety of methods have been developed to tackle the <a href="/wiki/Protein%E2%80%93protein_docking" title="Protein–protein docking" class="mw-redirect">protein–protein docking</a> problem, though it seems that there is still much work to be done in this field.</p> 
     <p>Other interactions encountered in the field include Protein–ligand (including drug) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Protein%E2%80%93peptide&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Protein–peptide (page does not exist)">protein–peptide</a>. Molecular dynamic simulation of movement of atoms about rotatable bonds is the fundamental principle behind computational <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a>, termed docking algorithms, for studying <a href="/wiki/Interactome" title="Interactome">molecular interactions</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_analysis">Literature analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Literature analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Text_mining" title="Text mining">Text mining</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_text_mining" title="Biomedical text mining">Biomedical text mining</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The growth in the number of published literature makes it virtually impossible to read every paper, resulting in disjointed sub-fields of research. Literature analysis aims to employ computational and statistical linguistics to mine this growing library of text resources. For example:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Abbreviation recognition – identify the long-form and abbreviation of biological terms</li> 
      <li>Named entity recognition – recognizing biological terms such as gene names</li> 
      <li>Protein-protein interaction – identify which <a href="/wiki/Proteins" title="Proteins" class="mw-redirect">proteins</a> interact with which proteins from text</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The area of research draws from <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computational_linguistics" title="Computational linguistics">computational linguistics</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-throughput_image_analysis">High-throughput image analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: High-throughput image analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Computational technologies are used to accelerate or fully automate the processing, quantification and analysis of large amounts of high-information-content <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">biomedical imagery</a>. Modern image analysis systems augment an observer's ability to make measurements from a large or complex set of images, by improving <a href="/wiki/Accuracy" title="Accuracy" class="mw-redirect">accuracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Objectivity_(science)" title="Objectivity (science)">objectivity</a>, or speed. A fully developed analysis system may completely replace the observer. Although these systems are not unique to biomedical imagery, biomedical imaging is becoming more important for both <a href="/wiki/Diagnostics" title="Diagnostics" class="mw-redirect">diagnostics</a> and research. Some examples are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>high-throughput and high-fidelity quantification and sub-cellular localization (<a href="/wiki/High-content_screening" title="High-content screening">high-content screening</a>, cytohistopathology, <a href="/wiki/Bioimage_informatics" title="Bioimage informatics">Bioimage informatics</a>)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Morphometrics" title="Morphometrics">morphometrics</a></li> 
      <li>clinical image analysis and visualization</li> 
      <li>determining the real-time air-flow patterns in breathing lungs of living animals</li> 
      <li>quantifying occlusion size in real-time imagery from the development of and recovery during arterial injury</li> 
      <li>making behavioral observations from extended video recordings of laboratory animals</li> 
      <li>infrared measurements for metabolic activity determination</li> 
      <li>inferring clone overlaps in <a href="/wiki/Gene_mapping" title="Gene mapping">DNA mapping</a>, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Sulston_score" title="Sulston score">Sulston score</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-throughput_single_cell_data_analysis">High-throughput single cell data analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: High-throughput single cell data analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Flow_cytometry_bioinformatics" title="Flow cytometry bioinformatics">Flow cytometry bioinformatics</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Computational techniques are used to analyse high-throughput, low-measurement single cell data, such as that obtained from <a href="/wiki/Flow_cytometry" title="Flow cytometry">flow cytometry</a>. These methods typically involve finding populations of cells that are relevant to a particular disease state or experimental condition.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_informatics">Biodiversity informatics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Biodiversity informatics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_informatics" title="Biodiversity informatics">Biodiversity informatics</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Biodiversity informatics deals with the collection and analysis of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> data, such as <a href="/wiki/Taxonomic_database" title="Taxonomic database">taxonomic databases</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Microbiome" title="Microbiome" class="mw-redirect">microbiome</a> data. Examples of such analyses include <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetics" title="Phylogenetics">phylogenetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niche_modelling" title="Niche modelling" class="mw-redirect">niche modelling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Species_richness" title="Species richness">species richness</a> mapping, or <a href="/wiki/Speciesism" title="Speciesism">species</a> identification tools.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Databases">Databases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Databases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_biological_databases" title="List of biological databases">List of biological databases</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Biological_database" title="Biological database">Biological database</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Databases are essential for bioinformatics research and applications. There is a huge number of available databases covering almost everything from DNA and protein sequences, molecular structures, to phenotypes and biodiversity. Databases generally fall into one of three types. Some contain data resulting directly from empirical methods such as gene knockouts. Others consist of predicted data, and most contain data from both sources. There are meta-databases that incorporate data compiled from multiple other databases. Some others are specialized, such as those specific to an organism. These databases vary in their format, way of accession and whether they are public or not. Some of the most commonly used databases are listed below. For a more comprehensive list, please check the link at the beginning of the subsection.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Used in <a href="/wiki/Sequence_motif" title="Sequence motif">Motif</a> Finding: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.genome.jp/tools/motif/">GenomeNet MOTIF Search</a></li> 
      <li>Used in Gene Ontology: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://toppgene.cchmc.org">ToppGene</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://llama.mshri.on.ca/cgi/func/funcassociate">FuncAssociate</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://amp.pharm.mssm.edu/Enrichr/">Enrichr</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gather.genome.duke.edu">GATHER</a></li> 
      <li>Used in Gene Finding: <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Markov_Model" title="Hidden Markov Model" class="mw-redirect">Hidden Markov Model</a></li> 
      <li>Used in finding Protein Structures/Family: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pfam.xfam.org/">PFAM</a></li> 
      <li>Used for Next Generation Sequencing: (Not database but data format), <a href="/w/index.php?title=FASTQ_Format&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FASTQ Format (page does not exist)">FASTQ Format</a></li> 
      <li>Used in Gene Expression Analysis: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/geo/">GEO</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/arrayexpress/">ArrayExpress</a></li> 
      <li>Used in Network Analysis: Interaction Analysis Databases(<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thebiogrid.org/">BioGRID</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mint.bio.uniroma2.it/mint/">MINT</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hprd.org/">HPRD</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cancer-systemsbiology.org/datasoftware.htm/">Curated Human Signaling Network</a>), Functional Networks (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://string.embl.de/%20">STRING</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.kegg.jp/kegg/pathway.html">KEGG</a>)</li> 
      <li>Used in design of synthetic genetic circuits: <a href="/wiki/GenoCAD" title="GenoCAD">GenoCAD</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Please keep in mind that this is a quick sampling and generally most computation data is supported by wet lab data as well.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_and_tools">Software and tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Software and tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">Software</a> tools for bioinformatics range from simple command-line tools, to more complex graphical programs and standalone web-services available from various <a href="/wiki/List_of_bioinformatics_companies" title="List of bioinformatics companies">bioinformatics companies</a> or public institutions.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open-source_bioinformatics_software">Open-source bioinformatics software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Open-source bioinformatics software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Many <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> tools have existed and continued to grow since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-obf-main_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obf-main-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The combination of a continued need for new <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> for the analysis of emerging types of biological readouts, the potential for innovative <i><a href="/wiki/In_silico" title="In silico">in silico</a></i> experiments, and freely available <a href="/wiki/Open_code" title="Open code" class="mw-redirect">open code</a> bases have helped to create opportunities for all research groups to contribute to both bioinformatics and the range of open-source software available, regardless of their funding arrangements. The open source tools often act as incubators of ideas, or community-supported <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-ins</a> in commercial applications. They may also provide <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> standards and shared object models for assisting with the challenge of bioinformation integration.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_bioinformatics_software" title="List of open-source bioinformatics software">range of open-source software packages</a> includes titles such as <a href="/wiki/Bioconductor" title="Bioconductor">Bioconductor</a>, <a href="/wiki/BioPerl" title="BioPerl">BioPerl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biopython" title="Biopython">Biopython</a>, <a href="/wiki/BioJava" title="BioJava">BioJava</a>, <a href="/wiki/BioJS" title="BioJS">BioJS</a>, <a href="/wiki/BioRuby" title="BioRuby">BioRuby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bioclipse" title="Bioclipse">Bioclipse</a>, <a href="/wiki/EMBOSS" title="EMBOSS">EMBOSS</a>, <a href="/wiki/.NET_Bio" title=".NET Bio">.NET Bio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(software)" title="Orange (software)">Orange</a> with its bioinformatics add-on, <a href="/wiki/Apache_Taverna" title="Apache Taverna">Apache Taverna</a>, <a href="/wiki/UGENE" title="UGENE">UGENE</a> and <a href="/wiki/GenoCAD" title="GenoCAD">GenoCAD</a>. To maintain this tradition and create further opportunities, the non-profit <a href="/wiki/Open_Bioinformatics_Foundation" title="Open Bioinformatics Foundation">Open Bioinformatics Foundation</a><sup id="cite_ref-obf-main_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obf-main-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> have supported the annual <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics_Open_Source_Conference" title="Bioinformatics Open Source Conference">Bioinformatics Open Source Conference</a> (BOSC) since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-obf-bosc_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obf-bosc-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>An alternative method to build public bioinformatics databases is to use the MediaWiki engine with the <a class="external text" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Extension:WikiOpener"><i>WikiOpener</i></a> extension. This system allows the database to be accessed and updated by all experts in the field.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Web_services_in_bioinformatics">Web services in bioinformatics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Web services in bioinformatics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/SOAP" title="SOAP">SOAP</a>- and <a href="/wiki/REST" title="REST" class="mw-redirect">REST</a>-based interfaces have been developed for a wide variety of bioinformatics applications allowing an application running on one computer in one part of the world to use algorithms, data and computing resources on servers in other parts of the world. The main advantages derive from the fact that end users do not have to deal with software and database maintenance overheads.</p> 
     <p>Basic bioinformatics services are classified by the <a href="/wiki/European_Bioinformatics_Institute" title="European Bioinformatics Institute">EBI</a> into three categories: <a href="/wiki/Sequence_alignment_software" title="Sequence alignment software" class="mw-redirect">SSS</a> (Sequence Search Services), <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sequence_alignment" title="Multiple sequence alignment">MSA</a> (Multiple Sequence Alignment), and <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics#Sequence_analysis" title="Bioinformatics">BSA</a> (Biological Sequence Analysis).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The availability of these <a href="/wiki/Service-orientation" title="Service-orientation">service-oriented</a> bioinformatics resources demonstrate the applicability of web-based bioinformatics solutions, and range from a collection of standalone tools with a common data format under a single, standalone or web-based interface, to integrative, distributed and extensible <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics_workflow_management_systems" title="Bioinformatics workflow management systems" class="mw-redirect">bioinformatics workflow management systems</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bioinformatics_workflow_management_systems">Bioinformatics workflow management systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Bioinformatics workflow management systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics_workflow_management_systems" title="Bioinformatics workflow management systems" class="mw-redirect">Bioinformatics workflow management systems</a>
     </div> 
     <p>A <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics_workflow_management_systems" title="Bioinformatics workflow management systems" class="mw-redirect">Bioinformatics workflow management system</a> is a specialized form of a <a href="/wiki/Workflow_management_system" title="Workflow management system">workflow management system</a> designed specifically to compose and execute a series of computational or data manipulation steps, or a workflow, in a Bioinformatics application. Such systems are designed to</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>provide an easy-to-use environment for individual application scientists themselves to create their own workflows</li> 
      <li>provide interactive tools for the scientists enabling them to execute their workflows and view their results in real-time</li> 
      <li>simplify the process of sharing and reusing workflows between the scientists.</li> 
      <li>enable scientists to track the <a href="/wiki/Provenance" title="Provenance">provenance</a> of the workflow execution results and the workflow creation steps.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Some of the platforms giving this service: <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_(computational_biology)" title="Galaxy (computational biology)">Galaxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kepler_scientific_workflow_system" title="Kepler scientific workflow system">Kepler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apache_Taverna" title="Apache Taverna">Taverna</a>, <a href="/wiki/UGENE" title="UGENE">UGENE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anduril_(workflow_engine)" title="Anduril (workflow engine)">Anduril</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_platforms">Education platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Software platforms designed to teach bioinformatics concepts and methods include <a href="/wiki/Rosalind_(education_platform)" title="Rosalind (education platform)">Rosalind</a> and online courses offered through the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Institute_of_Bioinformatics" title="Swiss Institute of Bioinformatics">Swiss Institute of Bioinformatics</a> Training Portal. The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Bioinformatics_Workshops" title="Canadian Bioinformatics Workshops">Canadian Bioinformatics Workshops</a> provides videos and slides from training workshops on their website under a <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> license. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://4273pi.org/">The 4273π project</a> or <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://4273pi.org/">4273pi</a> project <sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> also offers open source educational materials for free. The course runs on low cost raspberry pi computers and has been used to teach adults and school pupils.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> 4273π is actively developed by a consortium of academics and research staff who have run research level bioinformatics using raspberry pi computers and the 4273π operating system.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences">Conferences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioinformatics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Conferences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>There are several large conferences that are concerned with bioinformatics. Some of the most notable examples are <a href="/wiki/Intelligent_Systems_for_Molecular_Biology" title="Intelligent Systems for Molecular Biology">Intelligent Systems for Molecular Biology</a> (ISMB), <a href="/wiki/European_Conference_on_Computational_Biology" title="European Conference on Computational Biology">European Conference on Computational Biology</a> (ECCB), and <a href="/wiki/Research_in_Computational_Molecular_Biology" title="Research in Computational Molecular Biology">Research in Computational Molecular Biology</a> (RECOMB).</p>

       <li><cite class="citation journal">Gilbert D (2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bib.oxfordjournals.org/cgi/content/abstract/5/3/300">"Bioinformatics software resources"</a>. <i>Briefings in Bioinformatics</i> <b>5</b> (3): 300–304. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1093%2Fbib%2F5.3.300">10.1093/bib/5.3.300</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier" class="mw-redirect">PMID</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15383216">15383216</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABioinformatics&amp;rft.atitle=Bioinformatics+software+resources&amp;rft.au=Gilbert+D&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbib.oxfordjournals.org%2Fcgi%2Fcontent%2Fabstract%2F5%2F3%2F300&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1093%2Fbib%2F5.3.300&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F15383216&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.jtitle=Briefings+in+Bioinformatics&amp;rft.pages=300-304&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=5" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></li> 
       <li>Keedwell, E., <i>Intelligent Bioinformatics: The Application of Artificial Intelligence Techniques to Bioinformatics Problems</i>. Wiley, 2005. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0470021756" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-470-02175-6</a></li> 
       <li>Kohane, et al. <i>Microarrays for an Integrative Genomics.</i> The MIT Press, 2002. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/026211271X" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-262-11271-X</a></li>
